<date>1571864887128<//date><Rate>5< /Rate><review>Haven't been to this place in YEARS, but I'm so glad we stopped in for some lunch today. My wife and I sat at the bar and were immediately greeted by the bartender Evy. She was friendly and attentive our entire stay. They have a great selection of draft beer! I was stoked to see Coronado Blonde on draft. I had the Steak Bites, which were awesome and my wife had the Oriental Salad, which she loved. She would recommend you get the dressing on the side though. The vinaigrette on the salad  is delicious, but can pool at the bottom of the dish, so best to get it on the side. There were a few other people at the bar and the manager (Angela I believe was her name) was out on the floor talking it up with the customers. She stopped by and asked us how everything was. <user_name>Lori Jellison< /user_name><Time>1496441769039< /Time><rating>3</rating>< Text>
We've been coming to Cass St. Bar & Grill for years, and it's always been a casual bar (nothing fancy), but had great food (fresh fish, etc) for reasonable prices. However, the prices keep going up, and now they are at the point we expect a lot more for the price. The food isn't quite as good as it use to be, it cost more than it should ($12-13 for a salad), and there seemed to be a lot of confusion between the workers on how to pay. The stools are completely worn out (terribly torn & wobly), some tables are very sloped (to the point that another customers beer slid off onto the floor while the guy was up placing his order). Not sure what's going on, but they need to  sink a little money back into the place and get it back to the way it use to be.< /Text>

<time>1417725542922</time><rate>5< /rate><Text>This is one of the reviews that I don't really want to write so that it stays some what under the radar.

Cass St is where you can find good beer for reasonable prices, regulars who are always up for a game of pool, shuffleboard (but it gets crowded) and GREAT bar food. I highly recommend the cioppino and chicken baguette for lunch or dinner. Cass has my favorite cioppino in San Diego and for a much better price than other places! The main fish will vary based on their fish of the day (check the board) but comes with shrimp, muscles and clams. It's also worth getting the extra garlic bread!

They also have a great and diverse breakfast menu. I've been known to split the burrito between two meals! Don't forget a pitcher of mimosas which contains two, yes two, bottles of champagne!< /Text><pics>None< /pics>< Resp>

I love spice, and I love chicken so whenever I see a place that has spicy chicken I'm going to try it. I ordered the chicken sandwich and fried pickles. Since I was headed to work I only got the extra hot. For sure next time I'll order Get Clucked.

The sandwich was juicy and delicious. For me extra hot was mild, but I have a high tolerance for heat. I think the sauce would be great on fries. I can't wait to try Get Clucked. The portion of fried pickles was enough to satisfy two people. They are definitely worth the money. This place is on my list of favorites for spicy chicken.

Dine in still isn't allowed yet, but there's plenty of tables outside. The place is clean, and all COVID protocols are followed. I think some spicy chicken would be perfect to take on a flight. It would drive the other passengers nuts<//Text>

<user_name>Thomas Pichler</user_name><date>1619542136314<//date><Rating>5< /Rating>< Review>
This place is the epitome of human evolution.

I come here about twice a week and the food has always exceeded my expectations. Regardless if you like spicy food or not there is a heat level for everyone. My wife loves their country fried, while I am addicted to the extra hot.

Their portion sizes are huge as well. I still remember my first time here. I was absolutely speechless and had to sleep in my car for 30 minutes in the parking lot because the size of the sandwich knocked me out. Yes, It's huge.

As far as the sides go my favorites are the Corn Fritters and the Mac and Cheese. Their fries are of the curly kind but slightly on the salty side. Also, most of their sides are big enough to be shared, unless you are like me and vaporize a whole box by yourself.

Their cocktails are delicious too. You might be reserved ordering them since you do have to drive home after but I can assure you, after that size of a meal you could jug 8 of them and barely feel it.

Don't walk, run over here and get their food. Just don't do it when I am there, to keep the line short.< /Review>

<Name>Tyler M<//Name></record>
</dataset><record>
< Resp>
None<//Resp>
<Pics>[{'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipMniH66MGUYaOpLzz3ZSY3TFfGeV5GWPKZfVPpY=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipPKjaxdQe8IxG3ql6VGG-VC0wyjraMx5iixzTat=w150-h150-k-no-p']}, {'url': ['https://lh5.googleusercontent.com/p/AF1QipN14ApZZ1PUNQI3Ez9VfOocOU1mu9_QUfXGihU-=w150-h150-k-no-p']}]< /Pics><user_id>114322507478579427274</user_id><Rate>5<//Rate>< review>
Finally! Hot Chicken is back in the OC! Located near the SNA airport, this place serves bomb hot chicken and amazing sides. Most fried chicken joints do not have notable sides but Cluck takes their sides to the next level, I think I would even go here for the sides alone.

Warning for avid food lovers. Portion sizes are huge! I wanted to order a variety off the menu but it was a huge struggle to finish everything. Sauce portions are also huge. I would always run out of sauce when I get fried chicken but I had ample left after my meal.

I got the wings, tenders, sandwich, and fritters and pickle sides. All the chicken was super juicy and full of flavor. The skin is crispy and not overly bready. I'm also not sure what kind of chicken this place uses but the wings here are huge! They're about 2x the size of other chicken wings and I thought it might have been a turkey-chicken hybrid. Still tastes like bomb chicken though. But the sides are what really make this place. The corn fritters are almost like corn bread puffs and they are full of southern spices and bits of corn. This was bomb. I can imagine people coming here just to eat the fritters. Normally I don't like fried pickles but the frying took away some of the sourness of normal pickles. They taste almost like fried chicken coins with a bit of tang. Everything here was good!

There are five levels of spiciness and you can get mild or medium if you can't handle the heat. I went with Hot for all my orders and although I could taste the spice, I wasn't dieing or drenched in sweat. Would definitely go for the next level of Extra Hot next time.

Tip: I would recommend eating the chicken fresh or as soon as you can after you pick up your order. I took it home afterwards and let it sit for a while. Some of the chicken got soggy, especially the Tenders. Still good, but prolly would have been better if I didn't let it sit.< /review>

Really excellent! Our large group got some of almost everything (Nashville, Havarti, and regular chicken sandwiches, chicken fingers, fried pickles, corn fritters). Everyone loved their food. <Review>I would choose this restaurant over Chick-Fil-A any day.

Absolutely a delight. Since going to Nashville I have missed the hot chicken sandwich and this sandwich satisfied that craving. Their spice definitely has some kick and for optimal mouth feel and flavor eat it fresh.

Sandwiches/Meat (that I tried):
Nashville Hot: classic and delicious, on the spicier side but still has all the components I enjoy. Juicy, moist delicious and well cooked. A bit on the pricey side BUT you can tell it is cooked with love and care (the chicken is thick).

Havarti Hen: a unique take on a fried chicken sandwich but in my opinion was too sweet for my taste, I could see this flavor appealing to other people.

Tenders: So much food. This in my opinion is the best deal. The tenders are large and not overtly battered but still have a nice crunch and taste. Tried it with all the sauces I had and it worked with all of them. Forget Chick-fil-A, this is a MUCH better deal and tastes fresher.

Wing: Decent size, decent amount of meat, definitely the order for someone who likes bone-in chicken. Otherwise, I would say the tenders are better.

Based on the mayo I've tried and chicken quality, I expect the original to be nothing short of delicious.

Sides (that I tried):
Fried pickles: crispy and delicious, they don't skimp on the batter or the pickle, the ranch it comes with is also delicious. TIP: if you're not eating it right away, open the box to release the steam so it doesn't get soggy.

Corn Fritters: Super super crisp and fluffy, not too heavy on the palette and good flavor. The mayo included is delicious as well.

Mac & Cheese: The least unique thing in my opinion, but it's perfect for the kids and satisfies the purpose.

Fries: Curly fries that are crispy and curly, not much that's unique but closest resemblance is if the McDonald's French Fry and In-N-Out French fry had a baby.

Sauces (that I tried):
Cluck Sauce: The better of the two custom sauces. It's like ranchy and creamy and flavorful. Can't really put my finger on the exact flavor.
Comeback Sauce: A lesser Cane's sauce in my opinion, much more mayo-y than I would've liked and blander than the Cluck Sauce.

Lastly, price and ambiance. The staff was very friendly and you could tell they enjoyed where they worked. The restaurant itself is well designed and trendy, I can't wait to go eat there when indoor dining opens again. As for the price, I see that there are people who say that it's expensive and yes, it kinda is in comparison to fast-food fast food but for a fast casual restaurant I would say it's on-par/slightly above. BUT this is the restaurant's only location so be cognizant that it is a small business. If you like the food, and find the price in your budget, continue to support.

Will be back.< /Review><Pics>None<//Pics>< Rating>
5</Rating>

<Text>I constantly look for a good pizza and have not quite found it yet in the Desert after 35 years of being here.  I have not tried the pizza at the Haus yet because I have thoroughly enjoyed the soup, salad, subs and the â€œghetti.â€

The minestrone soup was just the right consistency â€“ not watery and not too thick, with just the right proportionate amount of the vegetables.  The salad that came with the soup combo was fresh, with no brown lettuce, and the garlic bread served with the combo is the best â€“ soft, yet crunchy and garlicky.The subs are tasty with generous portions of the meat/cheese.  The â€œghetti â€œsauce was the best ever.  Everything beat my current haunt, Mario's, by 26 miles.  I have back to the Haus 3 times in a week and look forward to the pizza on my soon-to-be next visit.

< user>
104501891651972235149<//user>
< Name>
CJ Glynn< /Name>
<time>1491067338741< /time><Rating>4<//Rating>< review>
Neither fancy, nor formal, Haus of Pizza is a local favorite for a reason: it puts out some great pizza.

Tucked in a strip mall off Highway 111, it would be easy to miss Haus of Pizza, and that would be a mistake.

The small dining room is nothing to behold: formica toped tables and linoleum floors.  But one does not come to Haus of Pizza for the atmosphere--it's the pizza that's the star.  The pies are neither Neapolitan thin crust, Chicago deep dish, nor New York style; they are medium thickness with good, yeasty dough, quality tomato sauce, and the list of usual suspects for ingredients, but are absolutely delicious.  The signature Haus Special pizza (medium, $15) with pepperoni, mushrooms, onions, olives, and sausage is a stand out.

While pizza is the star, Haus has other selections as well.  The generously proportioned chicken Parmesan sandwich (9-inch, $7.65) was hearty and filling.  The spaghetti and meatballs ($7.40) was very good; the sauce had great tomato flavor, and the meatballs were tender enough to cut with a fork.

Wine aficionados will be disappointed, as the selections are quite limited, but beer drinkers will be thrilled with the small (20 ounces) or large (32 ounces) chilled stone mugs and a good variety of beers on tap.

Service was fast, friendly, and efficient.  Kara, the hostess, cashier, and waitress makes juggling multiple tables, answering the constantly ringing telephone, and serving patrons at the counter look easy.

All in all, this "hole in the wall" serves fines pizza at very reasonable prices.  haus of Pizza is a must visit, if you are in Palm Desert.< /review>
